المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة

قوله: (استواء الطرفين والواسطة المراد من الطرفين والواسطة القرون ومن الاستواء الاستواء في الكثرة وامتناع تواطؤهم على الكذب . وقيل : المراد بالطرفين والواسطة المخبر الأول والثاني والثالث وبالاستواء هو الاستواء في احتمال قولهم للصدق والكذب فإن العلم يختلف باختلاف المخبرين، كما أنه يختلف بالوقائع فينبغي استواء المخبر الأول والذي بعده بالغاً ما بلغ والعلم به ممتنع والوجه الأول هو المفهوم من نهاية العقول والثاني هو المناسب لنفي إيجاب التواتر للعلم مطلقاً أي سواء كان في قرون أو قرن واحد، فتأمل.
قوله : ( عندنا معاشر الأشاعرة إلخ يمكن منع تساوي طبقات الأعداد من غير بنائه على أصل الأشاعرة لما يرى من قوة العشرة على مالا تقوى عليه الخمسة والثمانية . قوله : ( فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد قد يقال : لا شك أن نسبة قدرته تعالى إلى خلق العلم عقيب كل من تلك الطبقات على السوية، نعم قد يخلق عقيب البعض دون بعض آخر بحسب مشيئته وإرادته وذلك لا ينافي كون الطبقات متساوية في الاحتمال المذكور في حدود أنفسها، وأنت خبير بأنه يمكن رجع منع التساوي المذكور في الكتاب إلى هذا أيضاً، فتدبر.
قوله : (ضروري عندا لا نظري إنما قال: عندنا لأن الكعبي وأبا الحسين ذهب إلى أنه نظري زاعمين أن حصول العلم بالتواتر موقوف على استحضار مقدمتين الأولى أن الخبر الدال لا السنة قوم يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، والثانية أن كل خبر شأنه ذلك فهو صادق . والجواب المنع فإن الخبر إذا بلغ حد التواتر يعلم مضمونه قطعاً من غير ملاحظة لصدق الخبر ولا معرفة بلوغه حد التواتر بالفعل فضلاً عن استحصال ذلك العلم منهما ولذلك يحصل العلم به للصبيان الذين لا اهتداء لهم بطريق الاكتساب وترتيب المقدمات .
The First Observatory - The Third Objective: On the Possibility of the Mission (al-ba‘tha). The unanimity of its people by agreement from us and from you (rather the tawātur (mutual transmission) occurs) by one report after another, so the cause for it, i.e., for knowledge, on the supposition of its occurrence, is only) the last report) alone is what, along with what preceded it, because it has passed, so the report of one has then produced knowledge. (Fourth: its condition is the equality of the two ends and the middle) no matter how far they go (and there is no way to know it, i.e., the mentioned condition; and if the condition of its producing knowledge is not known, then knowledge is not obtained from it. Fifth: Indeed tawātur is not fixed by a specific number (rather its criterion with you is the occurrence of knowledge (of it, so that when knowledge of it occurs, it is known that it is tawātur; thus, it is not known to be tawātur except after knowledge of it occurs; so proving knowledge of it, i.e., of tawātur, is a petition of the question (muṣādara) and a clear vicious circle (dawr ṣarīḥ). And the answer to the first: denial of the equality of the judgment of the whole) in terms of its being a whole to the judgment of each individual, because we see the strength of ten in moving what each individual cannot move. And) the answer to the second: that the occurrence of knowledge with it, i.e., with tawātur, with us) the Ash‘arites, is only by the creation of God, Exalted is He, and He may create it by a number without another number; so we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers in the possibility of lying and its not producing knowledge. (Moreover, it, i.e., the occurrence of knowledge by way of tawātur of reports, differs according to the events, the reporters, and the hearers); so knowledge may occur in one event by a specific number and not occur by it in another event; and it may occur by the reports of specific groups and not occur by the reports of other groups equal to them in number; and likewise knowledge occurs for one hearer from a number and does not occur for another hearer from that number. (And) the answer to the third: as for us, it is because it, i.e., knowledge consequent to tawātur, is by the creation of God, so He may create it after the reports of a number without a single isolated report, so the last report is not a cause for it. (And as for the philosophers and the Mu‘tazila, because the reports) issued from the people of tawātur (are preparatory causes) for the occurrence of knowledge, not efficient causes; and they, i.e., the preparatory causes, may not accompany the effect but rather precede it, like movement for arriving at the destination. So the previous reports have an input in the occurrence of knowledge like the last report, and its agent is something else. This aspect suits the principles of the philosophers, and what suits the principles of the Mu‘tazila is what he mentioned by his saying: (Then we considered that the first report yields a conjecture (ẓann) and that conjecture is strengthened by the second and third, and so on until it reaches what is stronger than it, so it follows that the cause is the last report with the condition of the precedence of its likes); and that is what is meant by tawātur being productive of knowledge, so it does not follow that the isolated report of one is a cause for it. (And) the answer to the fourth and fifth: we claim necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī) obtained from actual tawātur under its condition and its criterion, for we use tawātur and knowledge of its condition and criterion as evidence for what we claim, and the difference between the two matters is apparent; for the occurrence of tawātur in actuality including the conditions considered in it and its production of necessary knowledge of that about which reports have been successively transmitted is a matter about which there is no doubt, since there is no way to necessary knowledge of distant lands and past persons except tawātur, and that knowledge is not considered by the condition which is equality, so that it is said: it is unknown, nor by knowledge of its criterion, so that a vicious circle would result. Yes, if one uses as evidence for something that its reports are tawātur including conditions gathered with its criterion, then what you mentioned—of lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the condition and the necessity of a vicious circle—is valid, but the knowledge derived from tawātur is necessary with us, not theoretical; so reflect.
His saying: (Equality of the two ends and the middle—what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the generations, and by equality is equality in multitude and the impossibility of their conspiring to lie. And it is said: what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the first, second, and third reporter, and by equality is equality in the possibility of their statements being true or false; for knowledge differs according to the difference of reporters, just as it differs according to events; so it is necessary that the first reporter and the one after him, no matter how far, be equal, and knowledge of it is impossible. The first aspect is what is understood from Nihāyat al-‘Uqūl, and the second is appropriate for negating the obligatoriness of tawātur for knowledge absolutely, i.e., whether it is in generations or one generation; so ponder.
His saying: (With us the Ash‘arites, etc.)—it is possible to deny the equality of the levels of numbers without building it on the principle of the Ash‘arites, because of what is seen of the strength of ten over what five and eight cannot. His saying: (So we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers)—it may be said: there is no doubt that the ratio of His power, Exalted, to creating knowledge consequent to each of those levels is equal; yes, He may create it consequent to some and not to others according to His will and intention, and that does not contradict the levels being equal in the mentioned probability in themselves. And you are aware that it is possible to refer the denial of the mentioned equality in the book to this as well, so reflect.
His saying: (Necessary with us, not theoretical)—he only said: with us because al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn held that it is theoretical, claiming that the occurrence of knowledge through tawātur depends on adducing two premises: first, that the report indicates that a group of people can be imagined to conspire to lie; second, that every report of that nature is truthful. And the answer is denial; for when a report reaches the level of tawātur, its content is known with certainty without observing the truthfulness of the report or knowing that it has actually reached the level of tawātur, let alone deriving that knowledge from them; and therefore knowledge of it is obtained by children who have no guidance to the method of acquisition and ordering of premises.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a series of Ash‘arite refutations of objections against the epistemological validity of tawātur (mutual transmission) as a source of certain knowledge. The author first presents two objections: the fourth objection claims that tawātur requires equality of the three generations, which is unknowable, so knowledge cannot arise; the fifth objection argues that tawātur's criterion is itself the occurrence of knowledge, leading to a vicious circle. The answer to the first objection denies that the whole is equal to its parts, using the analogy of ten people moving a weight that one cannot. The second answer explains that for Ash‘arites, knowledge occurs by God's direct creation, not by the numbers themselves, so the levels of numbers are not equal in producing knowledge—God may create knowledge from one number but not another, and it varies by event, reporter, and hearer. The third answer distinguishes between Ash‘arite and philosopher/Mu‘tazilite views: Ash‘arites hold that knowledge is created by God after reports, not caused by the last report alone; philosophers and Mu‘tazilites consider the reports as preparatory causes, with the last report serving as the efficient cause after a strengthening of conjecture. The answer to the fourth and fifth objections asserts that necessary knowledge from actual tawātur is self-evident, not dependent on knowing a theoretical condition or criterion; the knowledge is immediate and not subject to the charge of circularity. The subsequent glosses clarify key terms: 'equality of ends and middle' is interpreted as equality in generations or in probability; the denial of equality of numbers is compatible with God's equal power to create knowledge; and the final gloss explains why the Ash‘arites insist that tawātur knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī), refuting the view of al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn who considered it theoretical.

علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to refute the objection that the whole equals its parts?
A) A chain breaking at its weakest link
B) Ten people moving a weight one cannot
C) A single report being like a drop in an ocean
D) The impossibility of knowing the condition of equality

Key Takeaway
The collective strength of multiple reports produces certainty that a single report cannot, just as ten people can move what one alone cannot.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a collective testimony (like multiple witnesses to an event) because each individual seemed weak? How does this lesson challenge your tendency to undervalue collective strength? What change will you make in how you evaluate evidence about the Qur'an or Sunnah?
?
The strength of ten people moving a weight is not just additive but emergent. Where in your own practice of faith do you rely solely on individual efforts when collective action could achieve what seems impossible? Name one area you will commit to seeking jama'ah (community) for.
?
If you truly believe that Allah's preservation of the Qur'an through tawātur is a qualitative leap, not just many probabilities, how does that affect your confidence in its authenticity? Do you live as if that certainty is real, or do you still doubt? What step can you take today to strengthen that certainty?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
Knowledge by God’s Creation: The Second Objection Refuted
Ash‘arite refutation using God's creative act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash‘arites argue that knowledge from tawātur is directly created by God, not determined by number or equality of ranks.

Core Idea
God creates knowledge from tawātur as He wills, not by fixed numbers.

Another objection argues that the condition of equality (of ends and middle) is unknowable, so no knowledge can arise. The Ash‘arite response invokes God’s direct creation: He creates knowledge after some reports but not others, and it varies by event, reporter, and hearer. This lesson explains that variability.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the second answer
The objection claims the condition for tawātur (equality of generations in number and honesty) is unknowable. The answer says knowledge is created by God, so we do not need to know that condition. Read the passage carefully.
2
Understand the Ash‘arite principle of creation
For Ash‘arites, all knowledge is directly created by God. This means He can create it after any number of reports, independent of any inherent property of the reports.
This differs from views that rely on intrinsic causality.
3
Note the variability factors
The passage mentions knowledge differs by occurrence, reporters, and hearers. Reflect on why this is a powerful rebuttal: if knowledge were solely due to numbers, it would be uniform.

قوله : ( عندنا معاشر الأشاعرة إلخ يمكن منع تساوي طبقات الأعداد من غير بنائه على أصل الأشاعرة لما يرى من قوة العشرة على مالا تقوى عليه الخمسة والثمانية . قوله : ( فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد قد يقال : لا شك أن نسبة قدرته تعالى إلى خلق العلم عقيب كل من تلك الطبقات على السوية، نعم قد يخلق عقيب البعض دون بعض آخر بحسب مشيئته وإرادته وذلك لا ينافي كون الطبقات متساوية في الاحتمال المذكور في حدود أنفسها، وأنت خبير بأنه يمكن رجع منع التساوي المذكور في الكتاب إلى هذا أيضاً، فتدبر.
قوله : (ضروري عندا لا نظري إنما قال: عندنا لأن الكعبي وأبا الحسين ذهب إلى أنه نظري زاعمين أن حصول العلم بالتواتر موقوف على استحضار مقدمتين الأولى أن الخبر الدال لا السنة قوم يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، والثانية أن كل خبر شأنه ذلك فهو صادق . والجواب المنع فإن الخبر إذا بلغ حد التواتر يعلم مضمونه قطعاً من غير ملاحظة لصدق الخبر ولا معرفة بلوغه حد التواتر بالفعل فضلاً عن استحصال ذلك العلم منهما ولذلك يحصل العلم به للصبيان الذين لا اهتداء لهم بطريق الاكتساب وترتيب المقدمات .
The First Observatory - The Third Objective: On the Possibility of the Mission (al-ba‘tha). The unanimity of its people by agreement from us and from you (rather the tawātur (mutual transmission) occurs) by one report after another, so the cause for it, i.e., for knowledge, on the supposition of its occurrence, is only) the last report) alone is what, along with what preceded it, because it has passed, so the report of one has then produced knowledge. (Fourth: its condition is the equality of the two ends and the middle) no matter how far they go (and there is no way to know it, i.e., the mentioned condition; and if the condition of its producing knowledge is not known, then knowledge is not obtained from it. Fifth: Indeed tawātur is not fixed by a specific number (rather its criterion with you is the occurrence of knowledge (of it, so that when knowledge of it occurs, it is known that it is tawātur; thus, it is not known to be tawātur except after knowledge of it occurs; so proving knowledge of it, i.e., of tawātur, is a petition of the question (muṣādara) and a clear vicious circle (dawr ṣarīḥ). And the answer to the first: denial of the equality of the judgment of the whole) in terms of its being a whole to the judgment of each individual, because we see the strength of ten in moving what each individual cannot move. And) the answer to the second: that the occurrence of knowledge with it, i.e., with tawātur, with us) the Ash‘arites, is only by the creation of God, Exalted is He, and He may create it by a number without another number; so we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers in the possibility of lying and its not producing knowledge. (Moreover, it, i.e., the occurrence of knowledge by way of tawātur of reports, differs according to the events, the reporters, and the hearers); so knowledge may occur in one event by a specific number and not occur by it in another event; and it may occur by the reports of specific groups and not occur by the reports of other groups equal to them in number; and likewise knowledge occurs for one hearer from a number and does not occur for another hearer from that number. (And) the answer to the third: as for us, it is because it, i.e., knowledge consequent to tawātur, is by the creation of God, so He may create it after the reports of a number without a single isolated report, so the last report is not a cause for it. (And as for the philosophers and the Mu‘tazila, because the reports) issued from the people of tawātur (are preparatory causes) for the occurrence of knowledge, not efficient causes; and they, i.e., the preparatory causes, may not accompany the effect but rather precede it, like movement for arriving at the destination. So the previous reports have an input in the occurrence of knowledge like the last report, and its agent is something else. This aspect suits the principles of the philosophers, and what suits the principles of the Mu‘tazila is what he mentioned by his saying: (Then we considered that the first report yields a conjecture (ẓann) and that conjecture is strengthened by the second and third, and so on until it reaches what is stronger than it, so it follows that the cause is the last report with the condition of the precedence of its likes); and that is what is meant by tawātur being productive of knowledge, so it does not follow that the isolated report of one is a cause for it. (And) the answer to the fourth and fifth: we claim necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī) obtained from actual tawātur under its condition and its criterion, for we use tawātur and knowledge of its condition and criterion as evidence for what we claim, and the difference between the two matters is apparent; for the occurrence of tawātur in actuality including the conditions considered in it and its production of necessary knowledge of that about which reports have been successively transmitted is a matter about which there is no doubt, since there is no way to necessary knowledge of distant lands and past persons except tawātur, and that knowledge is not considered by the condition which is equality, so that it is said: it is unknown, nor by knowledge of its criterion, so that a vicious circle would result. Yes, if one uses as evidence for something that its reports are tawātur including conditions gathered with its criterion, then what you mentioned—of lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the condition and the necessity of a vicious circle—is valid, but the knowledge derived from tawātur is necessary with us, not theoretical; so reflect.
His saying: (Equality of the two ends and the middle—what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the generations, and by equality is equality in multitude and the impossibility of their conspiring to lie. And it is said: what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the first, second, and third reporter, and by equality is equality in the possibility of their statements being true or false; for knowledge differs according to the difference of reporters, just as it differs according to events; so it is necessary that the first reporter and the one after him, no matter how far, be equal, and knowledge of it is impossible. The first aspect is what is understood from Nihāyat al-‘Uqūl, and the second is appropriate for negating the obligatoriness of tawātur for knowledge absolutely, i.e., whether it is in generations or one generation; so ponder.
His saying: (With us the Ash‘arites, etc.)—it is possible to deny the equality of the levels of numbers without building it on the principle of the Ash‘arites, because of what is seen of the strength of ten over what five and eight cannot. His saying: (So we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers)—it may be said: there is no doubt that the ratio of His power, Exalted, to creating knowledge consequent to each of those levels is equal; yes, He may create it consequent to some and not to others according to His will and intention, and that does not contradict the levels being equal in the mentioned probability in themselves. And you are aware that it is possible to refer the denial of the mentioned equality in the book to this as well, so reflect.
His saying: (Necessary with us, not theoretical)—he only said: with us because al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn held that it is theoretical, claiming that the occurrence of knowledge through tawātur depends on adducing two premises: first, that the report indicates that a group of people can be imagined to conspire to lie; second, that every report of that nature is truthful. And the answer is denial; for when a report reaches the level of tawātur, its content is known with certainty without observing the truthfulness of the report or knowing that it has actually reached the level of tawātur, let alone deriving that knowledge from them; and therefore knowledge of it is obtained by children who have no guidance to the method of acquisition and ordering of premises.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a series of Ash‘arite refutations of objections against the epistemological validity of tawātur (mutual transmission) as a source of certain knowledge. The author first presents two objections: the fourth objection claims that tawātur requires equality of the three generations, which is unknowable, so knowledge cannot arise; the fifth objection argues that tawātur's criterion is itself the occurrence of knowledge, leading to a vicious circle. The answer to the first objection denies that the whole is equal to its parts, using the analogy of ten people moving a weight that one cannot. The second answer explains that for Ash‘arites, knowledge occurs by God's direct creation, not by the numbers themselves, so the levels of numbers are not equal in producing knowledge—God may create knowledge from one number but not another, and it varies by event, reporter, and hearer. The third answer distinguishes between Ash‘arite and philosopher/Mu‘tazilite views: Ash‘arites hold that knowledge is created by God after reports, not caused by the last report alone; philosophers and Mu‘tazilites consider the reports as preparatory causes, with the last report serving as the efficient cause after a strengthening of conjecture. The answer to the fourth and fifth objections asserts that necessary knowledge from actual tawātur is self-evident, not dependent on knowing a theoretical condition or criterion; the knowledge is immediate and not subject to the charge of circularity. The subsequent glosses clarify key terms: 'equality of ends and middle' is interpreted as equality in generations or in probability; the denial of equality of numbers is compatible with God's equal power to create knowledge; and the final gloss explains why the Ash‘arites insist that tawātur knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī), refuting the view of al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn who considered it theoretical.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash‘arite response, why does knowledge from tawātur differ by event, reporter, and hearer?
A) Because the condition of equality varies
B) Because God creates knowledge as He wills
C) Because reporters have different levels of honesty

Key Takeaway
Knowledge from tawātur is directly created by God and varies according to His will, not by any fixed condition or number.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a report that seems overwhelmingly confirmed (like from many sources), do you automatically trust it as absolute truth, or do you recognize that true certainty comes only if God creates it in your heart? How often do you actively pray for that divine creation of certainty?
?
If knowledge from tawātur is not automatic but depends on God's will, what does that mean for the certainty you feel about fundamental beliefs like the existence of God or the truth of the Quran? Is your confidence rooted in the number of proofs or in a personal awareness that God has granted you faith? What could you do to seek that gift more consciously?
?
The lesson shows that knowledge varies with the hearer—some receive certainty from a report while others do not. Have you ever been troubled by why some people fail to accept clear truths? How does this verse make you examine your own dependence on God's direct creation of knowledge, and what steps can you take to humble yourself before Him in seeking understanding?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
7 min
The Last Report as Cause: A Third Objection and Two Answers
Ash‘arite and Philosopher/Mu‘tazilite responses to the last-report objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the last report alone causes knowledge and the two different answers from the Ash‘arites and the Philosophers/Mu‘tazilites.

Core Idea
The last report is not the sole cause; either God creates knowledge or all reports are preparatory.

A third objection claims that if tawātur occurs gradually, only the last report can be the cause of knowledge. This lesson presents two refutations: the Ash‘arite view that God creates the knowledge, and the Philosopher/Mu‘tazilite view that earlier reports generate increasing conjecture, with the last report completing the process.

Guided Path
1
Read the third answer passage
The passage first gives the Ash‘arite answer, then the philosopher/Mu‘tazilite answer. Read both carefully.
The objection itself is implied but not given in the source chunk.
2
Compare the two answers
The Ash‘arite answer relies on direct divine creation. The other schools treat reports as preparatory causes (asbāb mu‘idda) that prepare the mind, with the last report being the efficient cause after strengthening conjecture.
Notice the difference in agency: God vs. natural causality.
3
Reflect on the strengthening of conjecture
The Mu‘tazilite explanation describes how the first report gives conjecture (ẓann), the second strengthens it, and so on until the last report produces certainty. This is a psychological accumulation.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة
اجتماع أهله اتفاقاً منا ومنكم ( بل يحصل ) التواتر ( بخبر واحد بعد واحد فالموجب له أي للعلم على تقدير حصوله إنما ) هو الخبر الأخير) وحده هو مع ما سبق لأنه قد انقضى فقد أفاد خبر الواحد العلم حينئذ . ( الرابع : شرطه استواء الطرفين والواسطة ) بالغة ما بلغت ( ولا سبيل إلى العلم به أي بالشرط المذكور وإذا لم يعلم شرط إفادته للعلم لم يحصل العلم منه الخامس : إن التواتر غير مضبوط بعدد معين (بل ضابطه عندكم حصول العلم (به حتى إذا حصل العلم به علم أنه متواتر فلا يعلم كونه متواتراً إلا بعد حصول العلم به فإثبات العلم به أي بالتواتر (مصادرة) على المطلوب ودور صريح ) وجواب الأول : منع مساواة حكم الكل) من حيث هو كل لحكم كل واحد لما نرى من قوة العشرة على تحريك ما لا يقوى عليه كل واحد و) . جواب ( الثاني أن حصول العلم عنده ) أي عند التواتر ( عندنا) معاشر الأشاعرة إنما هو ( بخلق الله تعالى إياه وقد يخلقه بعدد دون عدد فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد في احتمال الكذب وعدم إفادته العلم ( كيف وأنه ( أي حصول العلم بطريق تواتر الأخبار ( يختلف بالوقائع والمخبرين والسامعين) فقد يحصل العلم في واقعة بعدد مخصوص ولا يحصل به في واقعة أخرى وقد يحصل بأخبار جماعة مخصوصين ولا يحصل بأخبار جماعة أخرى تساويهم في العدد وكذا يحصل العلم لسامع من عدد ولا يحصل لسامع آخر من ذلك العدد ( و ) الجواب عن الثالث : أما عندنا فلانه ) أي العلم عقيب التواتر ( بخلق الله ) فقد يخلقه بعد أخبار عدد دون خبر واحد منفرد فلا يكون الخبر الأخير موجباً له ( وأما عند الحكماء والمعتزلة فلان الأخبار) الصادرة عن أهل التواتر ( أسباب معدة ) لحصول العلم لا موجبة له (وهي) أي الأسباب المعدة ( قد لا تجامع المسبب ) بل تكون متقدمة عليه ( كالحركة للحصول في المنتهي ) فللأخبار السابقة مدخل في حصول العلم كالخبر الأخير وفاعله شيء آخر وهذا الوجه يناسب أصول الحكماء والمناسب لأصول المعتزلة ما ذكره بقوله : (ثم أنفسنا أن الخبر الأول يفيد ظناً ويقوى ذلك الظن ( بالثاني والثالث ) وهكذا إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا أقوى منه فيلزم أن الموجب له هو الخبر الأخير بشرط سبق أمثاله ) وهو المراد بكون التواتر مفيداً للعلم فلا يلزم أن يكون خبر الواحد المنفرد موجباً له . (و) الجواب ) عن الرابع والخامس أنا ندعي العلم الضروري الحاصل من التواتر الواقع في نفس الأمر ) على شرطه ) وضابطه ) لأنا نستدل بالتواتر والعلم بحصول شرطه وضابطه ) على ما ادعيناه والفرق بين الأمرين (ظاهر) فإن حصول التواتر في نفس الأمر مشتملا على ما يعتبر فيه من الشرائط وإفادته للعلم الضروري بما تواتر الأخبار عنه أمر لا شبهة فيه إذ لا سبيل إلى العلم الضروري بالبلاد النائية والأشخاص الماضية سوى التواتر وليس يعتبر ذلك العلم بالشرط الذي هو الاستواء حتى يقال : إنه غير معلوم ولا العلم بضابطه حتى يلزم منه الدور ، نعم إذا استدل على شيء بكون أخباره متواترة مشتملة على شرائط مجتمعة مع ضابطه توجه ما ذكرتم من عدم العلم بحصول الشرط ومن لزوم الدور لكن العلم المستفاد من التواتر ضروري عندنا لا نظري فتدبر.
قوله: (استواء الطرفين والواسطة المراد من الطرفين والواسطة القرون ومن الاستواء الاستواء في الكثرة وامتناع تواطؤهم على الكذب . وقيل : المراد بالطرفين والواسطة المخبر الأول والثاني والثالث وبالاستواء هو الاستواء في احتمال قولهم للصدق والكذب فإن العلم يختلف باختلاف المخبرين، كما أنه يختلف بالوقائع فينبغي استواء المخبر الأول والذي بعده بالغاً ما بلغ والعلم به ممتنع والوجه الأول هو المفهوم من نهاية العقول والثاني هو المناسب لنفي إيجاب التواتر للعلم مطلقاً أي سواء كان في قرون أو قرن واحد، فتأمل.
قوله : ( عندنا معاشر الأشاعرة إلخ يمكن منع تساوي طبقات الأعداد من غير بنائه على أصل الأشاعرة لما يرى من قوة العشرة على مالا تقوى عليه الخمسة والثمانية . قوله : ( فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد قد يقال : لا شك أن نسبة قدرته تعالى إلى خلق العلم عقيب كل من تلك الطبقات على السوية، نعم قد يخلق عقيب البعض دون بعض آخر بحسب مشيئته وإرادته وذلك لا ينافي كون الطبقات متساوية في الاحتمال المذكور في حدود أنفسها، وأنت خبير بأنه يمكن رجع منع التساوي المذكور في الكتاب إلى هذا أيضاً، فتدبر.
قوله : (ضروري عندا لا نظري إنما قال: عندنا لأن الكعبي وأبا الحسين ذهب إلى أنه نظري زاعمين أن حصول العلم بالتواتر موقوف على استحضار مقدمتين الأولى أن الخبر الدال لا السنة قوم يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، والثانية أن كل خبر شأنه ذلك فهو صادق . والجواب المنع فإن الخبر إذا بلغ حد التواتر يعلم مضمونه قطعاً من غير ملاحظة لصدق الخبر ولا معرفة بلوغه حد التواتر بالفعل فضلاً عن استحصال ذلك العلم منهما ولذلك يحصل العلم به للصبيان الذين لا اهتداء لهم بطريق الاكتساب وترتيب المقدمات .
The First Observatory - The Third Objective: On the Possibility of the Mission (al-ba‘tha). The unanimity of its people by agreement from us and from you (rather the tawātur (mutual transmission) occurs) by one report after another, so the cause for it, i.e., for knowledge, on the supposition of its occurrence, is only) the last report) alone is what, along with what preceded it, because it has passed, so the report of one has then produced knowledge. (Fourth: its condition is the equality of the two ends and the middle) no matter how far they go (and there is no way to know it, i.e., the mentioned condition; and if the condition of its producing knowledge is not known, then knowledge is not obtained from it. Fifth: Indeed tawātur is not fixed by a specific number (rather its criterion with you is the occurrence of knowledge (of it, so that when knowledge of it occurs, it is known that it is tawātur; thus, it is not known to be tawātur except after knowledge of it occurs; so proving knowledge of it, i.e., of tawātur, is a petition of the question (muṣādara) and a clear vicious circle (dawr ṣarīḥ). And the answer to the first: denial of the equality of the judgment of the whole) in terms of its being a whole to the judgment of each individual, because we see the strength of ten in moving what each individual cannot move. And) the answer to the second: that the occurrence of knowledge with it, i.e., with tawātur, with us) the Ash‘arites, is only by the creation of God, Exalted is He, and He may create it by a number without another number; so we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers in the possibility of lying and its not producing knowledge. (Moreover, it, i.e., the occurrence of knowledge by way of tawātur of reports, differs according to the events, the reporters, and the hearers); so knowledge may occur in one event by a specific number and not occur by it in another event; and it may occur by the reports of specific groups and not occur by the reports of other groups equal to them in number; and likewise knowledge occurs for one hearer from a number and does not occur for another hearer from that number. (And) the answer to the third: as for us, it is because it, i.e., knowledge consequent to tawātur, is by the creation of God, so He may create it after the reports of a number without a single isolated report, so the last report is not a cause for it. (And as for the philosophers and the Mu‘tazila, because the reports) issued from the people of tawātur (are preparatory causes) for the occurrence of knowledge, not efficient causes; and they, i.e., the preparatory causes, may not accompany the effect but rather precede it, like movement for arriving at the destination. So the previous reports have an input in the occurrence of knowledge like the last report, and its agent is something else. This aspect suits the principles of the philosophers, and what suits the principles of the Mu‘tazila is what he mentioned by his saying: (Then we considered that the first report yields a conjecture (ẓann) and that conjecture is strengthened by the second and third, and so on until it reaches what is stronger than it, so it follows that the cause is the last report with the condition of the precedence of its likes); and that is what is meant by tawātur being productive of knowledge, so it does not follow that the isolated report of one is a cause for it. (And) the answer to the fourth and fifth: we claim necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī) obtained from actual tawātur under its condition and its criterion, for we use tawātur and knowledge of its condition and criterion as evidence for what we claim, and the difference between the two matters is apparent; for the occurrence of tawātur in actuality including the conditions considered in it and its production of necessary knowledge of that about which reports have been successively transmitted is a matter about which there is no doubt, since there is no way to necessary knowledge of distant lands and past persons except tawātur, and that knowledge is not considered by the condition which is equality, so that it is said: it is unknown, nor by knowledge of its criterion, so that a vicious circle would result. Yes, if one uses as evidence for something that its reports are tawātur including conditions gathered with its criterion, then what you mentioned—of lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the condition and the necessity of a vicious circle—is valid, but the knowledge derived from tawātur is necessary with us, not theoretical; so reflect.
His saying: (Equality of the two ends and the middle—what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the generations, and by equality is equality in multitude and the impossibility of their conspiring to lie. And it is said: what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the first, second, and third reporter, and by equality is equality in the possibility of their statements being true or false; for knowledge differs according to the difference of reporters, just as it differs according to events; so it is necessary that the first reporter and the one after him, no matter how far, be equal, and knowledge of it is impossible. The first aspect is what is understood from Nihāyat al-‘Uqūl, and the second is appropriate for negating the obligatoriness of tawātur for knowledge absolutely, i.e., whether it is in generations or one generation; so ponder.
His saying: (With us the Ash‘arites, etc.)—it is possible to deny the equality of the levels of numbers without building it on the principle of the Ash‘arites, because of what is seen of the strength of ten over what five and eight cannot. His saying: (So we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers)—it may be said: there is no doubt that the ratio of His power, Exalted, to creating knowledge consequent to each of those levels is equal; yes, He may create it consequent to some and not to others according to His will and intention, and that does not contradict the levels being equal in the mentioned probability in themselves. And you are aware that it is possible to refer the denial of the mentioned equality in the book to this as well, so reflect.
His saying: (Necessary with us, not theoretical)—he only said: with us because al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn held that it is theoretical, claiming that the occurrence of knowledge through tawātur depends on adducing two premises: first, that the report indicates that a group of people can be imagined to conspire to lie; second, that every report of that nature is truthful. And the answer is denial; for when a report reaches the level of tawātur, its content is known with certainty without observing the truthfulness of the report or knowing that it has actually reached the level of tawātur, let alone deriving that knowledge from them; and therefore knowledge of it is obtained by children who have no guidance to the method of acquisition and ordering of premises.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a series of Ash‘arite refutations of objections against the epistemological validity of tawātur (mutual transmission) as a source of certain knowledge. The author first presents two objections: the fourth objection claims that tawātur requires equality of the three generations, which is unknowable, so knowledge cannot arise; the fifth objection argues that tawātur's criterion is itself the occurrence of knowledge, leading to a vicious circle. The answer to the first objection denies that the whole is equal to its parts, using the analogy of ten people moving a weight that one cannot. The second answer explains that for Ash‘arites, knowledge occurs by God's direct creation, not by the numbers themselves, so the levels of numbers are not equal in producing knowledge—God may create knowledge from one number but not another, and it varies by event, reporter, and hearer. The third answer distinguishes between Ash‘arite and philosopher/Mu‘tazilite views: Ash‘arites hold that knowledge is created by God after reports, not caused by the last report alone; philosophers and Mu‘tazilites consider the reports as preparatory causes, with the last report serving as the efficient cause after a strengthening of conjecture. The answer to the fourth and fifth objections asserts that necessary knowledge from actual tawātur is self-evident, not dependent on knowing a theoretical condition or criterion; the knowledge is immediate and not subject to the charge of circularity. The subsequent glosses clarify key terms: 'equality of ends and middle' is interpreted as equality in generations or in probability; the denial of equality of numbers is compatible with God's equal power to create knowledge; and the final gloss explains why the Ash‘arites insist that tawātur knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī), refuting the view of al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn who considered it theoretical.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the last report of a tawātur chain is the sole cause of knowledge.
Correction: The last report is only effective because it follows preceding reports; alone it would not cause knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu‘tazilite explanation, what is the role of the first few reports?
A) They produce certainty immediately
B) They give conjecture that strengthens with each report
C) They are irrelevant to the final knowledge
D) They are created by God

Key Takeaway
The last report in tawātur does not act alone; either God creates knowledge after a series, or earlier reports build up conjecture until the last one completes it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your pursuit of religious knowledge, do you often demand immediate certainty from a single proof, or do you humbly allow the truth to build gradually through multiple sources? How might you change your approach after reflecting on this lesson?
?
The Ash‘arite answer reminds you that ultimate knowledge comes from God's creation, not from your own reasoning. Does your daily learning—whether in religion or in life—reflect that dependence on God, or do you credit your own intellect? What one habit could you adopt to make that dependence real?
?
When you finally grasp a difficult truth, do you thank God for the path He laid out—the many small steps and the cumulative evidence—or do you assume the last argument alone convinced you? How would your humility and gratitude change if you sincerely acknowledged every preparatory cause along the way?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
8 min
Necessary Knowledge and the Charge of Circularity
Ash‘arite resolution of the circularity and unknowability objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash‘arite response to the objections that the condition of tawātur is unknowable and that defining it by the occurrence of knowledge leads to a vicious circle.

Core Idea
Actual tawātur gives necessary knowledge that is self-evident, not dependent on prior conditions.

The fourth and fifth objections claim that tawātur cannot be defined because its condition is unknowable, and that using the occurrence of knowledge as its criterion leads to a vicious circle. The Ash‘arite answer draws a crucial distinction: actual tawātur in reality produces necessary knowledge, and that knowledge is not based on knowing the condition or criterion theoretically. This lesson clarifies that difference.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth and fifth objections
The fourth objection says the condition (equality of ends and middle) is unknowable. The fifth says tawātur is not fixed by number, and its criterion (occurrence of knowledge) leads to a circle. Read the objections carefully.
2
Read the combined answer
The answer claims necessary knowledge from actual tawātur. It distinguishes between the actual occurrence of tawātur (which gives knowledge) and using tawātur as evidence (which might require knowing conditions).
3
Grasp the distinction
The key point: when we experience tawātur, we get knowledge directly, without needing to verify conditions. The circularity only arises if we try to prove something by tawātur, not in the direct acquisition of knowledge.
The final gloss adds that this knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī) not theoretical.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة
اجتماع أهله اتفاقاً منا ومنكم ( بل يحصل ) التواتر ( بخبر واحد بعد واحد فالموجب له أي للعلم على تقدير حصوله إنما ) هو الخبر الأخير) وحده هو مع ما سبق لأنه قد انقضى فقد أفاد خبر الواحد العلم حينئذ . ( الرابع : شرطه استواء الطرفين والواسطة ) بالغة ما بلغت ( ولا سبيل إلى العلم به أي بالشرط المذكور وإذا لم يعلم شرط إفادته للعلم لم يحصل العلم منه الخامس : إن التواتر غير مضبوط بعدد معين (بل ضابطه عندكم حصول العلم (به حتى إذا حصل العلم به علم أنه متواتر فلا يعلم كونه متواتراً إلا بعد حصول العلم به فإثبات العلم به أي بالتواتر (مصادرة) على المطلوب ودور صريح ) وجواب الأول : منع مساواة حكم الكل) من حيث هو كل لحكم كل واحد لما نرى من قوة العشرة على تحريك ما لا يقوى عليه كل واحد و) . جواب ( الثاني أن حصول العلم عنده ) أي عند التواتر ( عندنا) معاشر الأشاعرة إنما هو ( بخلق الله تعالى إياه وقد يخلقه بعدد دون عدد فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد في احتمال الكذب وعدم إفادته العلم ( كيف وأنه ( أي حصول العلم بطريق تواتر الأخبار ( يختلف بالوقائع والمخبرين والسامعين) فقد يحصل العلم في واقعة بعدد مخصوص ولا يحصل به في واقعة أخرى وقد يحصل بأخبار جماعة مخصوصين ولا يحصل بأخبار جماعة أخرى تساويهم في العدد وكذا يحصل العلم لسامع من عدد ولا يحصل لسامع آخر من ذلك العدد ( و ) الجواب عن الثالث : أما عندنا فلانه ) أي العلم عقيب التواتر ( بخلق الله ) فقد يخلقه بعد أخبار عدد دون خبر واحد منفرد فلا يكون الخبر الأخير موجباً له ( وأما عند الحكماء والمعتزلة فلان الأخبار) الصادرة عن أهل التواتر ( أسباب معدة ) لحصول العلم لا موجبة له (وهي) أي الأسباب المعدة ( قد لا تجامع المسبب ) بل تكون متقدمة عليه ( كالحركة للحصول في المنتهي ) فللأخبار السابقة مدخل في حصول العلم كالخبر الأخير وفاعله شيء آخر وهذا الوجه يناسب أصول الحكماء والمناسب لأصول المعتزلة ما ذكره بقوله : (ثم أنفسنا أن الخبر الأول يفيد ظناً ويقوى ذلك الظن ( بالثاني والثالث ) وهكذا إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا أقوى منه فيلزم أن الموجب له هو الخبر الأخير بشرط سبق أمثاله ) وهو المراد بكون التواتر مفيداً للعلم فلا يلزم أن يكون خبر الواحد المنفرد موجباً له . (و) الجواب ) عن الرابع والخامس أنا ندعي العلم الضروري الحاصل من التواتر الواقع في نفس الأمر ) على شرطه ) وضابطه ) لأنا نستدل بالتواتر والعلم بحصول شرطه وضابطه ) على ما ادعيناه والفرق بين الأمرين (ظاهر) فإن حصول التواتر في نفس الأمر مشتملا على ما يعتبر فيه من الشرائط وإفادته للعلم الضروري بما تواتر الأخبار عنه أمر لا شبهة فيه إذ لا سبيل إلى العلم الضروري بالبلاد النائية والأشخاص الماضية سوى التواتر وليس يعتبر ذلك العلم بالشرط الذي هو الاستواء حتى يقال : إنه غير معلوم ولا العلم بضابطه حتى يلزم منه الدور ، نعم إذا استدل على شيء بكون أخباره متواترة مشتملة على شرائط مجتمعة مع ضابطه توجه ما ذكرتم من عدم العلم بحصول الشرط ومن لزوم الدور لكن العلم المستفاد من التواتر ضروري عندنا لا نظري فتدبر.
قوله: (استواء الطرفين والواسطة المراد من الطرفين والواسطة القرون ومن الاستواء الاستواء في الكثرة وامتناع تواطؤهم على الكذب . وقيل : المراد بالطرفين والواسطة المخبر الأول والثاني والثالث وبالاستواء هو الاستواء في احتمال قولهم للصدق والكذب فإن العلم يختلف باختلاف المخبرين، كما أنه يختلف بالوقائع فينبغي استواء المخبر الأول والذي بعده بالغاً ما بلغ والعلم به ممتنع والوجه الأول هو المفهوم من نهاية العقول والثاني هو المناسب لنفي إيجاب التواتر للعلم مطلقاً أي سواء كان في قرون أو قرن واحد، فتأمل.
قوله : ( عندنا معاشر الأشاعرة إلخ يمكن منع تساوي طبقات الأعداد من غير بنائه على أصل الأشاعرة لما يرى من قوة العشرة على مالا تقوى عليه الخمسة والثمانية . قوله : ( فلا نسلم تساوي طبقات الأعداد قد يقال : لا شك أن نسبة قدرته تعالى إلى خلق العلم عقيب كل من تلك الطبقات على السوية، نعم قد يخلق عقيب البعض دون بعض آخر بحسب مشيئته وإرادته وذلك لا ينافي كون الطبقات متساوية في الاحتمال المذكور في حدود أنفسها، وأنت خبير بأنه يمكن رجع منع التساوي المذكور في الكتاب إلى هذا أيضاً، فتدبر.
قوله : (ضروري عندا لا نظري إنما قال: عندنا لأن الكعبي وأبا الحسين ذهب إلى أنه نظري زاعمين أن حصول العلم بالتواتر موقوف على استحضار مقدمتين الأولى أن الخبر الدال لا السنة قوم يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، والثانية أن كل خبر شأنه ذلك فهو صادق . والجواب المنع فإن الخبر إذا بلغ حد التواتر يعلم مضمونه قطعاً من غير ملاحظة لصدق الخبر ولا معرفة بلوغه حد التواتر بالفعل فضلاً عن استحصال ذلك العلم منهما ولذلك يحصل العلم به للصبيان الذين لا اهتداء لهم بطريق الاكتساب وترتيب المقدمات .
The First Observatory - The Third Objective: On the Possibility of the Mission (al-ba‘tha). The unanimity of its people by agreement from us and from you (rather the tawātur (mutual transmission) occurs) by one report after another, so the cause for it, i.e., for knowledge, on the supposition of its occurrence, is only) the last report) alone is what, along with what preceded it, because it has passed, so the report of one has then produced knowledge. (Fourth: its condition is the equality of the two ends and the middle) no matter how far they go (and there is no way to know it, i.e., the mentioned condition; and if the condition of its producing knowledge is not known, then knowledge is not obtained from it. Fifth: Indeed tawātur is not fixed by a specific number (rather its criterion with you is the occurrence of knowledge (of it, so that when knowledge of it occurs, it is known that it is tawātur; thus, it is not known to be tawātur except after knowledge of it occurs; so proving knowledge of it, i.e., of tawātur, is a petition of the question (muṣādara) and a clear vicious circle (dawr ṣarīḥ). And the answer to the first: denial of the equality of the judgment of the whole) in terms of its being a whole to the judgment of each individual, because we see the strength of ten in moving what each individual cannot move. And) the answer to the second: that the occurrence of knowledge with it, i.e., with tawātur, with us) the Ash‘arites, is only by the creation of God, Exalted is He, and He may create it by a number without another number; so we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers in the possibility of lying and its not producing knowledge. (Moreover, it, i.e., the occurrence of knowledge by way of tawātur of reports, differs according to the events, the reporters, and the hearers); so knowledge may occur in one event by a specific number and not occur by it in another event; and it may occur by the reports of specific groups and not occur by the reports of other groups equal to them in number; and likewise knowledge occurs for one hearer from a number and does not occur for another hearer from that number. (And) the answer to the third: as for us, it is because it, i.e., knowledge consequent to tawātur, is by the creation of God, so He may create it after the reports of a number without a single isolated report, so the last report is not a cause for it. (And as for the philosophers and the Mu‘tazila, because the reports) issued from the people of tawātur (are preparatory causes) for the occurrence of knowledge, not efficient causes; and they, i.e., the preparatory causes, may not accompany the effect but rather precede it, like movement for arriving at the destination. So the previous reports have an input in the occurrence of knowledge like the last report, and its agent is something else. This aspect suits the principles of the philosophers, and what suits the principles of the Mu‘tazila is what he mentioned by his saying: (Then we considered that the first report yields a conjecture (ẓann) and that conjecture is strengthened by the second and third, and so on until it reaches what is stronger than it, so it follows that the cause is the last report with the condition of the precedence of its likes); and that is what is meant by tawātur being productive of knowledge, so it does not follow that the isolated report of one is a cause for it. (And) the answer to the fourth and fifth: we claim necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī) obtained from actual tawātur under its condition and its criterion, for we use tawātur and knowledge of its condition and criterion as evidence for what we claim, and the difference between the two matters is apparent; for the occurrence of tawātur in actuality including the conditions considered in it and its production of necessary knowledge of that about which reports have been successively transmitted is a matter about which there is no doubt, since there is no way to necessary knowledge of distant lands and past persons except tawātur, and that knowledge is not considered by the condition which is equality, so that it is said: it is unknown, nor by knowledge of its criterion, so that a vicious circle would result. Yes, if one uses as evidence for something that its reports are tawātur including conditions gathered with its criterion, then what you mentioned—of lack of knowledge of the occurrence of the condition and the necessity of a vicious circle—is valid, but the knowledge derived from tawātur is necessary with us, not theoretical; so reflect.
His saying: (Equality of the two ends and the middle—what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the generations, and by equality is equality in multitude and the impossibility of their conspiring to lie. And it is said: what is meant by the two ends and the middle is the first, second, and third reporter, and by equality is equality in the possibility of their statements being true or false; for knowledge differs according to the difference of reporters, just as it differs according to events; so it is necessary that the first reporter and the one after him, no matter how far, be equal, and knowledge of it is impossible. The first aspect is what is understood from Nihāyat al-‘Uqūl, and the second is appropriate for negating the obligatoriness of tawātur for knowledge absolutely, i.e., whether it is in generations or one generation; so ponder.
His saying: (With us the Ash‘arites, etc.)—it is possible to deny the equality of the levels of numbers without building it on the principle of the Ash‘arites, because of what is seen of the strength of ten over what five and eight cannot. His saying: (So we do not affirm the equality of the levels of numbers)—it may be said: there is no doubt that the ratio of His power, Exalted, to creating knowledge consequent to each of those levels is equal; yes, He may create it consequent to some and not to others according to His will and intention, and that does not contradict the levels being equal in the mentioned probability in themselves. And you are aware that it is possible to refer the denial of the mentioned equality in the book to this as well, so reflect.
His saying: (Necessary with us, not theoretical)—he only said: with us because al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn held that it is theoretical, claiming that the occurrence of knowledge through tawātur depends on adducing two premises: first, that the report indicates that a group of people can be imagined to conspire to lie; second, that every report of that nature is truthful. And the answer is denial; for when a report reaches the level of tawātur, its content is known with certainty without observing the truthfulness of the report or knowing that it has actually reached the level of tawātur, let alone deriving that knowledge from them; and therefore knowledge of it is obtained by children who have no guidance to the method of acquisition and ordering of premises.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a series of Ash‘arite refutations of objections against the epistemological validity of tawātur (mutual transmission) as a source of certain knowledge. The author first presents two objections: the fourth objection claims that tawātur requires equality of the three generations, which is unknowable, so knowledge cannot arise; the fifth objection argues that tawātur's criterion is itself the occurrence of knowledge, leading to a vicious circle. The answer to the first objection denies that the whole is equal to its parts, using the analogy of ten people moving a weight that one cannot. The second answer explains that for Ash‘arites, knowledge occurs by God's direct creation, not by the numbers themselves, so the levels of numbers are not equal in producing knowledge—God may create knowledge from one number but not another, and it varies by event, reporter, and hearer. The third answer distinguishes between Ash‘arite and philosopher/Mu‘tazilite views: Ash‘arites hold that knowledge is created by God after reports, not caused by the last report alone; philosophers and Mu‘tazilites consider the reports as preparatory causes, with the last report serving as the efficient cause after a strengthening of conjecture. The answer to the fourth and fifth objections asserts that necessary knowledge from actual tawātur is self-evident, not dependent on knowing a theoretical condition or criterion; the knowledge is immediate and not subject to the charge of circularity. The subsequent glosses clarify key terms: 'equality of ends and middle' is interpreted as equality in generations or in probability; the denial of equality of numbers is compatible with God's equal power to create knowledge; and the final gloss explains why the Ash‘arites insist that tawātur knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī), refuting the view of al-Ka‘bī and Abū al-Ḥusayn who considered it theoretical.

Key Terms
علم ضروري
مصادرة
دور صريح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That knowledge from tawātur is theoretical and requires prior verification of its conditions.
Correction: The knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī) and arises directly from the experience of tawātur, without needing to check conditions.

Checkpoint
What is the key distinction the author makes in answering the fourth and fifth objections?
A) Between knowledge from tawātur and knowledge from isolated reports
B) Between actual tawātur in reality and using tawātur as evidence
C) Between necessary and theoretical knowledge
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Actual tawātur provides necessary, self-evident knowledge that does not require knowing its theoretical conditions or criteria.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you know the Prophet ﷺ existed, but have you ever stopped to ask yourself: is that knowledge based on your own verification of conditions, or is it something that has been imprinted on your heart by the sheer weight of testimony? If the latter, do you live as though that knowledge is truly necessary and undeniable, or do you treat it as a mere probability?
?
When you hear that tawātur gives necessary knowledge without needing to check its criteria, does your heart feel the certainty of the unseen reports you have received, or do you find yourself demanding extra proof before submitting? What would change in your daily life if you truly accepted that this knowledge is as self-evident as seeing with your own eyes?
?
Consider the fact that you know about distant lands and past nations only through tawātur. Does this lesson make you more grateful for the knowledge that Allah has made accessible to you without your effort? How can you use this understanding to strengthen your trust in the authentic reports of Islam, even when doubts arise?

Lexical Explanation of the Word 'Gharaniq'
Lexical definition of 'gharaniq' and its singular/plural forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the lexical meanings and forms of the word 'gharaniq' as used in classical Arabic, which is crucial for interpreting certain theological narratives.

Core Idea
The word 'gharaniq' has multiple meanings—a bird, a handsome man, or soft garments—depending on context.

This lesson explores the lexical background of the word 'gharaniq', which appears in a controversial narrative about the Prophet's alleged slip. Understanding its possible meanings helps clarify the intended sense in that story. We'll examine the singular and plural forms as given by the commentator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, noting the different voweling patterns for the singular forms. Then read the English translation to confirm your understanding.
Pay attention to the damma, fatha, and kasra markings.
2
Understand the primary meaning
The word originally denotes a water bird with a long neck. Recognize that it is used metaphorically for handsome men or soft garments.
This metaphorical usage is important for interpreting the story.
3
Learn the plural forms
Three plural forms are given: ghara'iq, gharaniq, and ghirniqa. Note that 'gharaniq' is the one used in the narrative.
The variety of plurals shows the word's flexibility in Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الغرنيق بضم الغين المعجمة وفتح النون من طير الماء طويل العنق، وإذا وصف به الرجال فواحدة غرنيق وغرنوق بكسر الغين وفتح النون فيهما وغرنوق بالضم وغرائق وهو الثياب الناعم والجمع الغرائق بالفتح والغرانيق والغرنقة.
Al-ghurnayq (with damma on the ghayn and fatha on the nun) is from the water birds with a long neck. If it is used to describe men, the singular is ghurnayq and ghurnuq (with kasra on the ghayn and fatha on the nun in both) and ghurnuq (with damma) and ghara'iq, and it means soft garments. The plural is ghara'iq (with fatha) and gharaniq and ghirniqa.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This is a lexical note explaining the word 'al-gharaniq' that appears in the previous story. It defines the singular forms and their meanings: it can refer to a long-necked water bird, or metaphorically to handsome men, or to soft garments. The various plural forms are also given, including the form 'gharaniq' used in the story. This linguistic clarification helps understand the possible interpretations of the verse 'those are the high gharaniq'.

A) A type of soft garment.

Key Takeaway
The word 'gharaniq' is a plural form with multiple possible meanings, ranging from a literal water bird to metaphorical handsome men or soft garments.

Refutation of the Opponent's Argument from Accidents: Only Individuating Accidents Restored
Response to opponent's argument from accidents: only individuating accidents needed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why only individuating accidents need to be restored for numerical identity, resolving the opponent's contradiction.

Core Idea
Numerical identity requires restoring only individuating accidents, not every accident.

This lesson tackles a subtle objection: if a resurrected body must be numerically identical to the original, it seems it would have to be restored in its original time—leading to contradiction. The author presents the argument and then offers a concise response that clarifies what is truly necessary for identity.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's argument
Carefully read the first part of the passage where the opponent reasons that numerical identity requires restoration of all accidents, including the time of origination.
Notice the logical chain: identity → all accidents → includes time → same time → initial creation, not restoration.
2
Identify the contradiction
The opponent claims that if the thing is restored in its original time, it would be an initial creation (mubtada') rather than a restored thing (mu'ad), which is a contradiction.
This contradiction is meant to refute the possibility of resurrection as the same individual.
3
Understand the author's response
The author replies that only 'individuating accidents' (al-'awāriḍ al-mushakhkhiṣa) need to be restored, not all accidents. The time of origination is not such an accident.
This response resolves the contradiction: the same individual can be restored without being in the original time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الاستدلال فهو من وجوه: الأول: إنما يكون المعاد معادا بعينه إذا أعيد بجميع عوارضه ومنها الوقت الذي كان فيه مبتدأ فيلزم أن يعاد في وقته الأول وكل ما وقع في وقته الأول فهو مبتدأ فيكون حينئذ مبتدأ من حيث أنه معاد هذا خلف الجواب إنما اللازم في إعادة الشيء بعينه إعادة عوارضه المشخصة.
As for inferential reasoning, it is from several angles. The first: The restored thing is the very same thing only if it is restored with all its accidents, including the time in which it was initiated. Then it would have to be restored in its first time, and everything that occurs in its first time is an initiated thing; thus it would be an initiated thing inasmuch as it is restored—this is a contradiction. The answer: What is necessarily required in restoring the very same thing is only the restoration of its individuating accidents.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents the opponent's first inferential argument and the author's concise response. The opponent argues that for a thing to be numerically identical after restoration, it must be restored with all its accidents, including its specific time of origination. This would entail restoration in that same time, but then it would be an initial creation, not a restoration—a contradiction. The author's response is that only 'individuating accidents' (العوارض المشخصة) need to be restored, not all accidents. The time of origination is not an individuating accident in the sense required; thus the restored thing can be the same without being restored in its original time. This resolves the contradiction.

Key Terms
العوارض المشخصة
المعاد
المبتدأ
الوقت الأول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think numerical identity requires restoration of all accidents, including the time of origination.
Correction: The author clarifies that only individuating accidents are necessary; time is not individuating.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is necessary for a thing to be restored as the very same thing?
A) Restoration of all its accidents
B) Restoration of its individuating accidents only
C) Restoration in its original time
D) Restoration of its matter

Key Takeaway
To preserve numerical identity in restoration, only individuating accidents must be restored, not every accident including time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your identity in the next life depends only on specific individuating accidents, what does that reveal about the things you currently use to define yourself—your status, appearance, or achievements? Which of these are mere accidents that will not follow you, and are you ready to let them go?
?
The opponent insisted that restoration must be identical in every detail, including time, leading to impossibility. In your own life, where do you demand that things remain exactly as they were—same relationships, same circumstances—and face inner contradiction when they change? How can you accept that identity can persist through change, as the lesson teaches?
?
Time is not an individuating accident. Your past mistakes, your former self, do not define your resurrected identity. Are you holding onto a version of yourself that is tied to a specific time, rather than trusting that what makes you ‘you’ in Allah's sight is deeper than any temporal circumstance? Will you repent from the sins of the past without dragging them into your future?

Second Khariji Proof from Qur'an 34:17 and Its Refutation
Al-Jurjani presents and refutes the second Khariji proof using Qur'an 34:17.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars interpret Qur'an 34:17 to refute the Khariji claim that major sinners are unbelievers.

Core Idea
The Qur'anic verse is about a specific requital, not all requital.

The Kharijites used a verse from Surah Saba' to argue that anyone who is punished must be an unbeliever. Al-Jurjani presents their proof and then dismantles it by showing that the verse cannot be taken literally. This lesson walks through the proof, the response, and the proper interpretation of the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the Khariji proof
Examine the Kharijites' argument: they cite Qur'an 34:17 and reason that since the verse says only the ungrateful are requited, and the major sinner is requited (punished), he must be an unbeliever.
Identify the key premise: requital is limited to unbelievers.
2
Study the first response
The apparent meaning of the verse is impossible because it would mean that believers who are rewarded are also ungrateful. This is false because believers are requited with reward.
The response points out that requital includes both reward and punishment.
3
Study the second response and conclusion
The confinement of requital to the ungrateful is also contradicted by other verses (e.g., 40:17) that say every soul is requited. Therefore, the verse must refer to a specific kind of requital exclusive to the ungrateful, as indicated by its context.
The major sinner may receive a different requital, so the proof fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( الثاني : ( من تلك الوجوه : قوله تعالى : وهل يجازي إلا الكفور ﴾ [سبأ : ۱۷] ) فإنه يدل على أنه كل من يجازى فهو كافر، وصاحب الكبيرة ممن يجازى لقوله: ﴿ ومن يقتل مؤمناً متعمداً فجزاؤه جهنم [ النساء : ٩٣ ] ، فيكون كافراً ، قلنا : ( هو ) متروك الظاهر) لأن ظاهره حصر الجزاء في الكفور وهو متروك قطعاً ( إذ يجازى غير الكفور وهو المثاب) لأن الجزاء يعم الثواب والعقاب، (و) أيضاً ذلك الحصر متروك لقوله تعالى : اليوم تجزى كل نفس بما كسبت ﴾ [غافر : ۱۷] ، فوجب حمل الآية على جزاء مخصوص بالكافر كما يدل عليه سياق الآية أعني قولك ذلك : جزيناهم بما كفروا ﴾ [سبأ: ۱۷]، فالمعنى وهل يجازى ذلك الجزاء إلا الكفور وصاحب الكبيرة جاز أن يجازى جزاء مغايراً لما يختص بالكافر .
The second: from those aspects: His statement, exalted is He, ‘And will any be requited except the ungrateful?’ (Saba' 34:17). For it indicates that everyone who is requited is an unbeliever, and the perpetrator of a major sin is among those who are requited because of His statement, ‘And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell’ (al-Nisa' 4:93), so he would be an unbeliever. We say: It is abrogated in its apparent meaning, because its apparent meaning confines requital to the ungrateful, and that is definitely abrogated, since other than the ungrateful are requited – namely the one who is rewarded – because requital encompasses both reward and punishment. Also, that confinement is abrogated by His statement, exalted is He, ‘Today every soul will be requited for what it has earned’ (Ghafir 40:17). So it is necessary to interpret the verse as referring to a requital specific to the unbeliever, as indicated by the context of the verse, namely His saying, ‘Thus We requited them because they disbelieved’ (Saba' 34:17). So the meaning is: ‘And will that particular requital be given except to the ungrateful?’ The perpetrator of a major sin may be requited with a requital different from that which is specific to the unbeliever.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage contains the second Khariji proof and the response. The Kharijites cite Qur'an 34:17, which asks 'And will any be requited except the ungrateful?', arguing that requital is restricted to the ungrateful (i.e., unbelievers). Since the major sinner is subject to requital (e.g., for intentional murder, the punishment is Hell), he must be an unbeliever. The response has two parts. First, the apparent meaning of the verse is that only the ungrateful are requited, but this is false because both believers and unbelievers are requited – believers with reward. Therefore the apparent meaning must be abandoned. Second, the verse's confinement is contradicted by other verses like 40:17 that state every soul is requited for its deeds. So the verse must be interpreted as referring to a specific kind of requital, namely the requital that is exclusive to the ungrateful, as indicated by the context: 'Thus We requited them because they disbelieved'. Thus the phrase means 'Will that specific requital be given except to the ungrateful?' The major sinner may receive a different requital (e.g., temporary punishment in Hell or other punishment distinct from the eternal punishment of the unbeliever). Hence the proof fails.

Key Terms
الجزاء
الكفور
المثاب
الظاهر
المتروك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves that anyone who is punished (requited) must be an unbeliever.
Correction: The verse is about a specific requital for ungratefulness, not all requital. Believers are also requited (with reward).

Checkpoint
How does the Ahl al-Sunna interpret Qur'an 34:17 ('And will any be requited except the ungrateful?')?
A) They accept it literally, so only unbelievers are punished
B) They interpret it as referring to a specific requital exclusive to unbelievers, not all requital
C) They say the verse is abrogated by another verse
D) They apply it only to the Jews

Key Takeaway
The second Khariji proof fails because the Qur'anic verse about requital does not apply to all requital but only to a specific requital reserved for the ungrateful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a Qur'anic verse that seems to condemn a group, do you immediately apply it to others without considering its context and specific meaning? What assumption about yourself does that reveal about your readiness to judge?
?
The Kharijites used a verse to declare major sinners as unbelievers. Are there any people in your life whom you have mentally 'written off' because of their sins? In light of this lesson, what might you be missing about God's specific requital for them?
?
The refutation relies on the fact that requital includes both punishment and reward. Do you live with a balanced awareness that God requites both good and evil, or do you focus only on His punishment? How does that affect your hope and gratitude toward Him?

Third Khariji Proof and Its Refutation
Al-Jurjani refutes the third Khariji proof using Qur'an 3:97 about Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna refuted the Khariji argument that neglecting Hajj constitutes unbelief, by distinguishing between denial of obligation and metaphorical usage.

Core Idea
Denying an obligation is kufr; neglecting it out of weakness is not.

In this passage, al-Jurjani addresses the third proof presented by the Kharijites, who claimed that failing to perform Hajj is equivalent to unbelief based on a verse from Surah Al 'Imran. He provides two clear rebuttals that protect the doctrine of irja' (postponement of judgment) regarding major sins. Let's examine how the verse is properly understood.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the Khariji interpretation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the Kharijites take the verse literally to claim that abandoning Hajj is kufr.
Focus on the phrase 'and whoever disbelieves' and how it is interpreted.
2
Understand the first response: denial of obligation
The first response clarifies that the verse refers to one who denies the obligation (juhud al-wujub) of Hajj, not one who neglects it. This is a key distinction in Islamic theology.
Denying a clear obligation is indeed unbelief, but mere failure to act is not.
3
Explore the second response: metaphorical usage
The second response suggests that the term 'kufr' might be used metaphorically to emphasize the gravity of neglecting Hajj, not as actual unbelief. This shows rhetorical subtlety in the Qur'an.
This explanation preserves the consistency of other texts that do not label the neglectful as kafir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( الثالث : قوله تعالى بعد إيجاب الحج ومن كفر ﴾ [آل عمران : ٩٧] أي لم يحج ( فإن الله غني عن العالمين) فقد جعل ترك الحج كفراً، (قلنا : المراد من جحد وجوبه ولا شك في كفره .
قوله : (قلنا : المراد من جحد وجوبه) وأيضاً يجوز أن يكون التعبير عن ترك الحج بالكفر بطريق الاستعارة استعظاماً له أو تغليظاً في الوعيد عليه .
The third: His statement, exalted is He, after making Hajj obligatory, 'And whoever disbelieves – then indeed, Allah is free from need of the worlds' (Al 'Imran 3:97), meaning whoever does not perform Hajj – so He made the abandonment of Hajj unbelief. We say: The intended meaning is the one who denies its obligation; there is no doubt about his unbelief. His statement: 'We say: the intended meaning is the one who denies its obligation' – and also it is possible that the expression of abandoning Hajj as unbelief is by way of metaphor, magnifying it or emphasising the warning against it.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the third Khariji proof. They cite the verse from Al 'Imran 3:97, which after commanding Hajj says 'And whoever disbelieves – then indeed, Allah is free from need of the worlds.' The Kharijites interpret 'whoever disbelieves' as 'whoever does not perform Hajj', thus making the major sinner (who neglects Hajj) an unbeliever. The response clarifies that the verse refers to the one who denies the obligation of Hajj, not the one who merely fails to perform it out of negligence. Denying an obligatory act is indeed unbelief. The commentator adds a second possible explanation: the word 'kufr' here could be metaphorical, used to emphasize the gravity of abandoning Hajj and to strongly warn against it, not to assert actual unbelief. This is a common rhetorical device in the Qur'an.

The Qur'anic phrase 'whoever disbelieves' in the Hajj verse refers to denial of obligation, not mere neglect, and even if interpreted as metaphor, it serves to emphasize the warning.
